## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in a material, which is fundamental to constitutive modeling. Temperature typically affects elastic modulus (thermal softening) and can activate plastic flow mechanisms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with temperature-dependent modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain for work hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook strength (isothermal): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (flow stress with hardening and thermal softening)
- Rubber/entropic elasticity: sigma = c0 * T * epsilon (stress proportional to temperature times strain)
- Neo-Hookean type: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**(-2)) (entropic elasticity for large deformations)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (coupled power-law in strain and temperature)
- Voce hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 - c1 * exp(-c2 * epsilon)) * (1 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (cubic polynomial constitutive law)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated deformation)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon) (sinh-type constitutive law, common in creep)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon - c1 * T (stress with thermal stress contribution)
- Ludwik equation with temperature: sigma = c0 * T**c1 * epsilon**c2 + c3 * epsilon (generalized power-law with temperature scaling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening ŌåÆ Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (1 - (c*T)**n) reducing stress at higher temperatures
- Entropic elasticity (rubber-like) ŌåÆ Stress proportional to T*epsilon, indicating entropy-driven restoring force
- Strain hardening saturation ŌåÆ Forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition ŌåÆ Stress as product of strain-dependent and temperature-dependent terms: f(epsilon)*g(T)
- Large deformation nonlinearity ŌåÆ Polynomial or power-law terms in strain beyond linear (epsilon**2, epsilon**3)
- Creep/viscoplastic flow ŌåÆ Hyperbolic sine sinh(c*epsilon) or inverse hyperbolic functions of stress
- Phase transition or abrupt softening ŌåÆ Sigmoidal temperature dependence like 1/(1+exp(c*(T-Tc))) indicating critical temperature
- Competing elastic and thermal stress ŌåÆ Additive structure c0*epsilon + c1*T representing mechanical vs thermal contributions
